  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText1568659752720304465" style="display:none"><b>THEY WILL BE TESTED</b><br /><br /><i>Sydney Sage is an Alchemist, one of a group of humans who dabble in magic and serve to bridge the worlds of humans and vampires. Meanwhile, she and Adrian becomes enmeshed in a puzzle that could hold the key to a shocking secret about spirit magic, a secret that could shake the entire Moroi world and alter their lives forever.<br /><br />Don't miss their unforgettable final chapter. . . .<br /><br /><b>LOVE WILL CONQUER ALL</b></span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's so nice to know I'm not alone! I usually don't read spin-off series and, like you, wasn't at all excited. But I so enjoyed reading from Sydney's <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's so nice to know I'm not alone! I usually don't read spin-off series and, like you, wasn't at all excited. But I so enjoyed reading from Sydney's point of view and Adrian is absolutely fantastic! I also really liked having Eddie as a bigger part of the story. As of right now, I'd say this is my new favorite series. I've read everything but The Ruby Circle at least twice.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1196339325" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196339325" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1196339325?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=bastard-hero">bastard-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=witchy-shit">witchy-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring-crap-hero">boring-crap-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring-main-characters">boring-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=die-book-die">die-book-die</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=daddy-issues-mummy-issues">daddy-issues-mummy-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=desperate-pathetic-heroine">desperate-pathetic-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=mary-sue-heroine">mary-sue-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=die-hero-die">die-hero-die</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1196339325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11489260074308599001"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>I'm glad the series is finally over, it's weird how much I used to enjoy it. I think my love for cheesy YA books has dwindled to nothing in the last year or so. They're just so predictable and trite, there's no originality, twists or turns, and the main characters and relationship dynamics are always the same. It's such lazy and formulaic writing. <br/><br/>-I missed the old Sydney, in the beginning of the series she was her own person, but by the end she was all about Adrian, it was clear that sh</span>
  <span id="freeText11489260074308599001" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />I'm glad the series is finally over, it's weird how much I used to enjoy it. I think my love for cheesy YA books has dwindled to nothing in the last year or so. They're just so predictable and trite, there's no originality, twists or turns, and the main characters and relationship dynamics are always the same. It's such lazy and formulaic writing. <br /><br />-I missed the old Sydney, in the beginning of the series she was her own person, but by the end she was all about Adrian, it was clear that she was just a special little snowflake specially built for Adrian. She used to actually be rather interesting and endearing, but she became a total shrew who did nothing but nag Adrian non-stop and bang on about him and their contrived, mushy love. She was seriously more like an overbearing mother than a girlfriend. <br />I wasn't impressed that the once ambitious Sydney who wanted to travel the world and had all sorts of dreams, instead got to be a dutiful teenage wife and mother. Sure, she got to go to college but the fact that she was a good little wifey and mummy when she was still a teenager pissed me the hell off. Heaven forbid a heroine ending up single and hopeful for the next chapter in their life. Nope, they have to be tied down to a guy and sometimes even a baby. Why do YA books shove the idea that a girl can only ever be truly happy unless she's practically married? <br />At least Dmitri and Adrian were into their twenties and had plenty of life and relationship experience when they settled down, unlike Sydney and Rose who ended up with the first guy they had proper relationships with. How ridiculous. <br /><br />-I hated Adrian, he was as immature and irritating as ever. He acted like a major brat with his tantrums and arguing. He wanted everyone to dance to his tune, and if he they didn't he'd sulk or feel sorry for himself, he was so pathetic.<br />I had to laugh at Adrian making a real effort to help find Jill and help Nina find her missing sister, when he couldn't even be bothered to do the same when Sydney was kidnapped and tortured. Nope, drinking, partying, cheating and flirting was more important than the so called loved of his life. Yet I was somehow meant to believe that he loved Sydney oh so much. Yea right.<br />Also, even though Adrian said he would risk his life for Sydney, his actions never really supported that. Even at the end when he was using spirit to help her fight that demon I never actually got the sense that he would physically risk his life for her (whereas she definitely would for him), even the spirit powers he used to save her didn't seem all that excessive (despite what he claimed). Sydney was always the one going into danger and risking her life whilst Adrian was always hanging back, chilling out and being coddled. It never once felt like Adrian would do for her what she would do for him. I hated them together, even though I'm no longer a fan of Sydney I still think she deserved so much better than him.<br /><br />-I didn't enjoy Adrian's POV whatsoever, I didn't care about Nina or Olive or his spirit powers. It was boring, whatever charm he once had was all but gone.<br /><br />-HATED all the forced Adrian and Sydney moments to make them seem cute and coupley.. Like the squirrel incident, the pie place, and looking after Declan. Ugh, it was so contrived and nauseating.<br /><br />-I didn't even like when Rose, Dmitri, Christian, or Lissa showed up. I used to love them popping up in and out of the series but they were so blah in this. I actually hated Rose with her 'slut shaming' of dhampir women that lived in communes, she was a stuck up, judgemental cow. Also, how did Dmitri know so much about dhampir communes unless he'd gone there himself and taken advantage of the dhampir women? With his track record of shagging schoolgirls I wouldn't put it past him.<br /><br />-I enjoyed the Alicia/witchy storyline when it was first introduced, I thought something fun or epic would happen with that arc, but it ended up being a damp squib. Alicia was a cookie cutter villain and there was never any doubt she would end up defeated. Also, the witches never really added anything relevant to the <i>VA</i> world. I've realised the sole purpose they were included in the first place wasn't to add to the world or for a thrilling plot. No, it was just so that Sydney would have powers, so she could properly be involved in the action scenes and actually be able to hold her own when it came to the bad guys. It was yet more lazy writing. <br /> <br />-What was the point of Olive's storyline beside letting Adrian and Sydney play mummy and daddy without Sydney actually getting pregnant? Oh that's right, it was also to get Nina (the other woman) out of the way and to give speshul snowflakes Dimtri and Rose a snowflake baby. Olive's whole character was just there to make Adrian/Sydney and Rose/Dimitri's relationships oh so perfect. Ugh. <br /><br />-Loved Daniella, Inez and Jackie. They were the most entertaining characters out of the lot. <br /><br />-Dimitri and Adrian cousins? Ugh, please. I refuse to believe Dmitri not knowing exactly who his dad was.<br /><br />-It was impossible to tell that Sydney had so recently undergone months of torture. There was barely any hint of it apart from her casually mentioning it once or twice. Her imprisonment and torture was obviously only done for some cheap drama and angst. If anything Adrian was the one who acted like he'd gone through major trauma, it didn't help that Sydney kept molly coddling him, she practically changed his nappies, fed him and burped him, their relationship was so off putting. <br /><br />-I was disappointed that the series didn't end up properly tackling the outdated moroi/dhampir dynamics, the racist Alchemists, the fanatical Warriors of Light, and the vile treatment of dhampir women. The <i>VA</i> world was so backwards and had so many issues, there was potential to address those and for the protagonists to really fight for progression and equal rights and something that mattered outside of themselves (instead of essentially fighting for teen love). Instead all they did was make half-arsed attempts at change or make no attempts whatsoever or ignore it entirely. It would have been unrealistic if everyone had suddenly become enlightened but some progression/education/forward thinking/change could have been implemented when it came to the Alchemists/moroi/dhampirs. The moroi possibly being able to fight and defend themselves, and re-education possibly-kind-of stopping one day was nowhere near good enough. <br />I'm still baffled as to why dhampirs/guardians are cool with being second class citizens. It doesn't matter if they grew up being told they were, they still had minds of their own and were living in the modern world (where millions had fought for equal rights for decades). Surely, some influential and forward thinking dhampirs would have wanted the same equality and fought for it by now? <br /><br />-And why were moroi so cool with their dhampir children risking their lives for them? Surely, most of them wouldn't want their kids putting their lives on the line to save a bunch of spoilt moroi. Hardly any parents would want their children dying to protect them, why would moroi be any different even if their kids are dhampirs?<br />Also, how were the Alchemists able to get away with their whole torture/re-education? Why didn't Lissa or the moroi demand they stop that? Sure, the Alchemists were their own organisation but the moroi must have had some say or power in the way they ran things since their job was directly related to them. <br /><br />-Also, why didn't Marcus or Sydney fight harder to try and change the Alchemist way? It was like they all just got on with their own lives and happily abandoned and ignored all the fucked up things that needed to be addressed. Sydney making one deal with the Alchemists wasn't nearly enough, she could have fought harder and longer or she could have helped from a distance. Her living it up with Adrian whilst her little sister was at the mercy of the sadistic Alchemists was quite disgusting. I didn't want her to be playing happy families, I wanted her to be out there fighting and taking down the Alchemists and making a change, instead her ending was totally insulting and uninspired. I expected Sydney (well pre-AdrianDatingSydney) to do far greater things.<br /><br />-The ending was over the top cheesy with babies and marriage for everyone. I rolled my eyes at Adrian becoming a devoted dad/husband after a lifetime of immaturity, partying, and dependency on others, it didn't ring true him becoming SuperDad. <br /><br />I wanted to like <i>The Ruby Circle</i> after enjoying most of the <i>VA/Bloodlines</i> series (bar the last couple of books).. But I think I've just become less tolerant and more cynical of YA that doesn't even try to be a little bit original, and instead sticks with the usual tropes and never surprises or shocks when it comes to plot, characters, or relationships. That said I think that fans of Adrian/Sydney and the series in general will probably enjoy this.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11489260074308599001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1745262046?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Poppy~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Poppy~" href="/user/show/59201076-poppy">~Poppy~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745262046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11145851707268645762"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Being with you is the best thing that's ever happened to me, the one perfect decision I've made in a lifetime of fumbling and poor judgment. I'd go through it all again to be by your side. Never doubt that. Never doubt how I feel about you.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455435637ra/18100723.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>

  </i>
</blockquote><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466708666ra/19510844.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495286478ra/22803715.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></span>

<div id="review_957280448" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/957280448" />
    <a title="Sakina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30464687-sakina"><img alt="Sakina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452366526p2/30464687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/957280448?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sakina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sakina" href="/user/show/30464687-sakina">Sakina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24578249-the-ruby-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30464687-sakina?shelf=heart-touching">heart-touching</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30464687-sakina?shelf=i-didn-t-see-that-coming">i-didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30464687-sakina?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30464687-sakina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30464687-sakina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30464687-sakina?shelf=captivating">captivating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30464687-sakina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30464687-sakina?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer957280448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14268683462193951786"><b>
  <u>After Reading</u>
</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1429968267p8/1173454.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So I finally read it! And I am so depressed and happy! The ending was beautiful yet I hate to say goodbye to this series. This review is really personal and sappy, so if you want skip reading it, I won't blame you.<br/><blockquote>
  <b>I felt her fear before I heard her screams.<b></b></b>
</blockquote><br/>This one line is enough to transport me 3 years back, when I bought my first book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9373792-vampire-academy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vampire Academy</a>. I was a late bloomer when it came to reading. 4 years back I started reading books, one in 2 months. I use to always pick u</span>
  <span id="freeText14268683462193951786" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>After Reading</u>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1429968267p8/1173454.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So I finally read it! And I am so depressed and happy! The ending was beautiful yet I hate to say goodbye to this series. This review is really personal and sappy, so if you want skip reading it, I won't blame you.<br><blockquote>
  <b>I felt her fear before I heard her screams.<b></b></b>
</blockquote><br>This one line is enough to transport me 3 years back, when I bought my first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9373792-vampire-academy" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a>. I was a late bloomer when it came to reading. 4 years back I started reading books, one in 2 months. I use to always pick up Vampire Academy when I visited the bookstore and upon my first reading the synopsis I thought it contained a love triangle between <b>Rose-Dimitri-Lissa.</b> Thinking back I have a good laugh. I never bought the book until 3 years back because I had nothing to read. <b>I started reading it and just like that I fell in love with books.</b><br><br>In the above pic a few books are missing, some have been lent and some like SS and TRC are on kindle because I couldn't buy the books since this way the collection is incomplete and thus not a constant reminder that the series is over. <br><blockquote>
  <b>Sydney: “the guy with you … the tall Moroi with dark hair … is that your boyfriend?”<br>Rose: “Er, yeah.”<br>Sydney: “He’s cute.”<br>Rose: “For an evil creature of the night?”</b>
</blockquote><br>I remember reading this and thinking, what if Sydney and Adrian got together? So imagine my surprise when I found out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8709527.Bloodlines__Bloodlines___1_" title="Bloodlines (Bloodlines, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloodlines</a> series was about them!!<br><blockquote>
  <b>“I don't balance you like you need."<br>"What the hell does that mean?" he exclaimed.<br>My heart ached for him, and I was so sorry for what I'd done...but this was the truth of it all. "The fact that you have to ask says it all. When you find that person...you'll know.” </b>
</blockquote><br>I remember reading this and hating Rose. I hated her so much. But now that is in the past. Looking back so much has happened and changed since VA till TRC. I have too many memories attached to both the series. Even though I have found many series that I love nothing will compare to <b>VA, BL and Pride and Prejudice.</b><br><br>The Ruby Circle, to be honest was a little boring at the beginning but it picked up pace and then it was series of twists and turns. Even though I am glad Rose and Dimitri were there, I was disappointed that Angeline was a no-show. I really liked her character. <br><br>Though the book lacked here and there, my love for this series, it's characters and that ending is enough for me to give this book 5 stars.<br><br>If you haven't read the series, I would recommend it. Many may not find the first book that interesting <s>and the movie was a disaster</s>(*whispers*it was) but the series does get better.<br><br><b>LOVE YOU VAMPIRE ACADEMY AND BLODDLINES &lt;3</b><br><br><u>
  <b>Before Reading</b>
</u><br><i>The <b>last</b> book in the Bloodlines series</i><br><br>My mind: "It's okay no need to cry, you knew this was coming." <br>Me: "Bu-But <i>no more</i> Sydrian, <i>no more</i> ADRIAN!! &lt;3 I-I can't help myself. I don't want this series to end!!"<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401864590ra/9860269.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Bloodlines series came into my life as a lighting bolt. It shattered my world. But it also remade it. <br>It gave me an opportunity to discover another side of Adrian which I had seen only in glimpses in VA but got a full understanding of in this series. I got a chance to know the real Adrian Ivashkov. <b>It made me love Adrian even more than I already did. I love him so much it hurts.</b></i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396486580ra/9141502.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It gave me ships like <i>Jeddie</i> and <i>Angeline-Trey</i> and also <i>Ms.T-Wolf.</i> It gave me Sydrian feels I couldn't handle especially in TFH. I don't think I'm ready to let this series or characters go. I don't think I'll ever be.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401864476ra/9860245.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14268683462193951786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_634027046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/634027046" />
    <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source"><img alt="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586156113p2/6511257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/634027046?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source">Sue (Hollywood News Source)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=paranormal-urban-fantasy">paranormal-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer634027046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7417310059631897789"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436806945i/15505344.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I survived reading The Ruby Circle. Can you believe it? I have battle wounds and I live to tell you this wondrous tale.<br/><br/><b>I know a half ass written book when I see one. The Ruby Circle is a train wreck waiting to happen since The Fiery Heart and I couldn’t get off fast enough.</b> <br/><br/>Despite its second rate book covers and questionable plot. I genuinely loved the first two books of Bloodlines series. The third book, <em>The Indigo Spell</em> isn’t as bad as the latter ones, but I don’t have a soft spot for it unli</span>
  <span id="freeText7417310059631897789" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436806945i/15505344.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I survived reading The Ruby Circle. Can you believe it? I have battle wounds and I live to tell you this wondrous tale.<br><br><b>I know a half ass written book when I see one. The Ruby Circle is a train wreck waiting to happen since The Fiery Heart and I couldn’t get off fast enough.</b> <br><br>Despite its second rate book covers and questionable plot. I genuinely loved the first two books of Bloodlines series. The third book, <em>The Indigo Spell</em> isn’t as bad as the latter ones, but I don’t have a soft spot for it unlike its prior installments. <b>The last three books, however is the downfall of the series.</b><br><br>Bloodlines follows the story of Sydney Sage, a teenager girl who is part of an Alchemist organization. They aim to prevent humans from discovering there is another species apart from them. When Sydney was sent to Palm Springs, California to oversee the protection of a <em>Moroi </em>Princess with a band of <em>Morois</em> and <em>Dhampirs</em>. She soon after discovers, vampires are not as evil and "creatures of the night" as her society taught her to be. As a result, Sydney started questioning everything she has learned.<br><br>Similarly to its two predecessors, The Ruby Circle is told from the shifting point of views of Adrian and Sydney. I don’t know why Mead ever thought adding Adrian’s POV is a necessary course direction. The first three books went very well without any of his input. The tricky thing about incorporating multiple POVs, they rarely work for me, especially for male narrators. The author is juggling too many plates. Case scenario: POV1 already covered what POV2 is currently lamenting. It doesn’t seem authentic to me. Of course, there are few authors who handled this fantastically with fluid and effective narrative, but Bloodlines series isn’t one of them. It was poorly executed. Adrian become whiny contrary to his character development. And Sydney lacked the gleam, I initially find so endearing.<br><br> <blockquote>
<strong>What Really Happened Throughout This Book:</strong><br><br>Adrian: Mom! Can you come here?<br><br>Daniella: Sure. Just give me a sec!<br><br><strong>(Daniella apparated in the next paragraph) </strong><br><br>*Adrian is in the court while Sydney is off fighting another weird species of demons*<br><br>*Sydney on the verge of getting annihilated*<br><br>*Adrian magically appears out of nowhere*<br><br>*Uses spirit magic to save Sydney*<br><br><b>Me: Amazing story telling skillz </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Besides from the lackluster narration of the novel, I am baffled by the direction of the plot. <strong>At this point, I didn’t even know where did it go?</strong> The Ruby Circle introduced plenty of obstacles and trials while Mead keeps springing unnecessary twists. They weren’t properly delivered. All the loose ends weren't neatly tied. It was cringe and cheese induced fest.<br><br>Adrian and Sydney was out of character, the supporting characters are cardboard cutout. <strong>There is no logical explanation for this bat shit trying hard for a book, other than I’ve read better Sydrian fanfics than this. </strong><br><br>I will not even breathe a word about the epilogue.<br><br>This series makes me extremely sad, because at point of my life, I was obsessed with these books. They deserved so much better than this. To say, I am disappointed would be the understatement of the century.<br><br><b>Overall, I am not recommending the last three books of this series to anyone. And to all Bloodlines fans who doesn’t have the courage to pick this up. I feel you and you’ve been a valiant soldier.</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7417310059631897789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-witches-and-wizards">fantasy-witches-and-wizards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=maybe-its-just-me">maybe-its-just-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=hot-guys-alphas-rawr">hot-guys-alphas-rawr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer764775642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9323745642532173072"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423713205ra/13662187.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Well, that was disappointing for the last book in this mostly really good series. There was one part in the middle of the book where I felt like it was going to be great, the pacing rocked, the action was cresting, revelations... then. The last half of the book was boring, cliched, and ended up with a very cheesy HEA for all.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423713206ra/13662188.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>There's no big spoilers below, but there may be what some consider minor "spoilerish" items included, if it matters to you.</b> <br/><br/>- I found Sydney very annoying in this book. By b</span>
  <span id="freeText9323745642532173072" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423713205ra/13662187.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, that was disappointing for the last book in this mostly really good series. There was one part in the middle of the book where I felt like it was going to be great, the pacing rocked, the action was cresting, revelations... then. The last half of the book was boring, cliched, and ended up with a very cheesy HEA for all.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423713206ra/13662188.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>There's no big spoilers below, but there may be what some consider minor "spoilerish" items included, if it matters to you.</b> <br><br>- I found Sydney very annoying in this book. By book 6, you'd think she would accept Adrian and his Spirit ability. But no, she is STILL constantly trying to get him on medication to sever his connection to Spirit when she should be helping him learn ways to use it and be stronger. SO freaking annoying.<br><br>- Richelle Mead has written every possible stereotype into this series. At first, I could deal because of Sydney's past. It made sense with her background and childhood. But now, it doesn't work anymore. Plus, it extends to other characters. Rose (yes, she is back in this) calls "blood whores" (dhampirs who give moroi sex and food/blood for affection and money and gifts - and <i>companionship</i>) "disgusting." Slut shaming. Rose (in Vampire Academy) was loving getting felt up and making out with guys, but she is still so quick to judge??? You'd think she would understand by now that it isn't cool to judge others. Plus, apparently, people who smoke marijuana are dumb idiots who eat nothing but Twinkies and junk food and can't remember what happened a minute ago. Not to mention the usual stuff that has been in every book - criticisms about eating/food, coffee, alcohol, any vice basically. I have to wonder if this is Richelle Mead speaking through the characters or if it's just a coincidence all her characters are so restrictive and judgmental.<br><br>- Sydney was always trying to refuse people's help. Like, her friends and people who care about her. Still doing it by book 6. No. No excuse anymore.<br><br>- Minor characters were brought back for no apparent reason and once again, it seems like an author tries to tie up every single loose end with a neat little bow.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423713206ra/13662189.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- The middle of the book had a great section (which is why I am not giving this 1 star). I was totally engaged. Then, it was like a second book started. A really boring one. The stupid Warriors came back and I never liked them. The whole last part was about a stupid scheme involving infiltrating them (again). It was boring and seemed like filler.<br><br>Honestly, Jill being kidnapped was never a good idea to base the last book in a series on. Jill is a sweet character, but I never cared so much about her that a whole plot focusing on her would intrigue me. A better story would have been about Sydney still running from the Alchemists or something involving her sister and father (who were only in it a little bit). Or helping Adrian master spirit to help find the cure to restore strigoi they've been looking for. (But instead we get the same tiresome phantom Aunt Tatiana voice in his head, trying to lead him to insanity.)<br><br>I was disappointed. I always liked this series because it seemed like the typical YA tropes weren't as overbearing. Sydney and Adrian were just so blah in this. I really didn't like Sydney at all. Adrian was tolerable, but in the end, Sydrian turned out so vanilla and boring and meh. <br><br>- Oh, how annoying that Sydney is still so grossed out by Adrian having to drink blood to survive. Seriously. She should be offering to feed him every once in awhile. This is another one of those instances where you have to wonder if the author even likes the idea of vampires, yet she has made a career off writing about them. There is really not much positive about them in this series. Still. By book 6. Same attitude, nothing has really changed. Sigh.<br><br>- Finally, after <b>12 books</b> in this world, absolutely NOTHING changed as far as the relationships between moroi, dhampirs, and humans (we saw small potential progress with the alchemists). Why wasn't any of this addressed? The species are still basically exactly the same in each others world. Dhampirs are basically servants and soldiers, the moroi still boss them around. No one seems to want change. <b>Still.</b> Dealing more with this would have been more interesting to me. Seeing more changes in their worlds. <br><br>I think I'm done with Richelle Mead.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423713206ra/13662190.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9323745642532173072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_734785615" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/734785615" />
    <a title="Glass" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4808910-glass"><img alt="Glass" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583244629p2/4808910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/734785615?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glass" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glass" href="/user/show/4808910-glass">Glass</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

We've been in this world for so long and it's nice to see it reaching this point but then I'll miss it. Still let's keep it where it is and let it go now.<br/><br/><b>Glass:</b> That is something I wholeheartedly agree with - Vampire Academy and Bloodlines fictional world should end here.   <span id="freeText2885109235883804860" style="display:none"><b>Review posted at <a href="http://jacitamati.blogspot.com/2015/02/the-ruby-circle-by-richelle-mead.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Ja čitam, a ti?</a></b><br><br><b>Glass:</b> We have been scared of this day. Last Bloodlines novel. What will we do with our lives now?<br><br><b>Tanja:</b> Yeah, I wonder the same. It's just damn bittersweet. We've been in this world for so long and it's nice to see it reaching this point but then I'll miss it. Still let's keep it where it is and let it go now.<br><br><b>Glass:</b> That is something I wholeheartedly agree with - Vampire Academy and Bloodlines fictional world should end here. We are a little bit biased when it comes to these books - our friendship actually started because of our shared love for Rose, Dimitri and Adrian. (We even named our little nephew Adrian.) That doesn't mean that we can't recognize bad sides of this story. Like how it started really slow and ending was rushed.<br><br><b>Tanja:</b> Exactly, especially after all that crescendo we went through at the end of Silver Shadows. For me it felt like stepping into anther story altogether at the start. I needed some getting used to the pace and plot line. (Even though, as always Mead didn't fail to repeat things, which still drives me crazy. I see point of it, but honestly it's not like someone will read this before any other book in both series and wouldn't know about dhampirs and moroi and all that).<br><br><b>Glass:</b> But she actually toned it down in final book, I was more annoyed by it in previous one.<br>What did you think about Sydney and Adrian? I know that you prefer Dimitri, but Adrian was always my favorite. He truly grow up in The Ruby Circle.<br><br><b>Tanja:</b> Oh I adore him too. I mean I always did, but it bothered me how immature he was in the previous books. I did like his boy charm and all, but now I think I fully grew to love him. I like how more serious and adult he became. Which is amazing in this series, as you really saw him change. Both him and Sydney, but I think it was more present in his character.<br><br><b>Glass:</b> Sydney was kind of consistent trough whole series - she is responsible, too mature for her age, ambitious, confident, smart and strong. That is why I loved her, she is not the most usual female character you can find in this type of books.<br>But the way everything ended and that epilogue! I just loved epilogue!<br><br><b>Tanja:</b> That thing was like cherry on top! I was kind of worried how all this will end, somehow the whole book was so rushed at the end that I was scared for the epilogue but then Mead did was I will always be grateful for. She combined the two and closed this world. Like I always say, we might have left this world, but parts of our hearts will still remain there. As it should be.<br><br>*************************************<br><b>How I imagine Adrian Ivashkov?</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423772898ra/13670638.gif" width="500" height="299" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423772898ra/13670640.gif" width="315" height="215" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1016155871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1016155871" />
    <a title="Stephanie (Bookfever)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4939266-stephanie-bookfever"><img alt="Stephanie (Bookfever)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595589358p2/4939266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1016155871?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie (Bookfever)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie (Bookfever)" href="/user/show/4939266-stephanie-bookfever">Stephanie (Bookfever)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=owned-physical-books">owned-physical-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=2015-publication">2015-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1016155871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17063753692771864135">The Ruby Circle was a amazing conclusion to a series that has meant a lot to me. For the last four years I was lucky enough to read books in this world and now that it has all ended I feel both glad and sad to have been on this journey. I'll miss these characters a lot - especially Adrian - but the ending couldn't have been more perfect. <br/><br/>As always I enjoyed reading about both Sydney and Adrian a lot. People who know me even a little bit know how much I love Adrian. These past years he's been my </span>
  <span id="freeText17063753692771864135" style="display:none">The Ruby Circle was a amazing conclusion to a series that has meant a lot to me. For the last four years I was lucky enough to read books in this world and now that it has all ended I feel both glad and sad to have been on this journey. I'll miss these characters a lot - especially Adrian - but the ending couldn't have been more perfect. <br><br>As always I enjoyed reading about both Sydney and Adrian a lot. People who know me even a little bit know how much I love Adrian. These past years he's been my favorite character and I can only applaud Richelle Mead for writing him and been able to see him grow and change (for the better) as a character, especially in the Bloodlines series. I'm pretty sure that everyone who's read both Vampire Academy and Bloodlines can agree that the Adrian we met in Frostbite (vampire academy #2) isn't the same guy that we've come to know through the Bloodlines series. And that's pretty remarkable. <br><br>But anyway, on to The Ruby Circle. I obviously loved it. Quite a few things got resolved and some unexpected twists (read the book and you'll know what I'm talking about) honestly freaked me out (in the best way!). I love Sydney and Adrian's relationship but right from the start it's very clear they have some issues that are unresolved. They both have flaws but they trust each other completely and they're both equally fierce in wanting to protect one another. I love them. <br><br>As it was the last Bloodlines book a lot familiar characters made an appearance. Rose and Dimitri were a pretty big part of the book. I always enjoy reading about them and knowing what's going on with them. Let's just say that I'm pleased with where their life is taking them with what I read at the ending. Of course other familiar people were in it, but I won't bore you with naming them all. <br><br>I also really liked the action, there was a lot of it in the book. Both Sydney and Adrian are pretty badass in their own way. Sydney with her magic and Adrian with his spirit magic (although I hated seeing what it did to his sanity). They might've not have a lot of time for romance but the moments they could steal together were intense, sweet and just absolute. <b>
  <i>The Center Will Hold!</i>
</b><br><br>As far as series endings go, The Ruby Circle is one of my favorites. I managed only just not to cry, but I was very emotional reading those last few pages. Of course I wish there would be more books coming or another spin-off but I think the ending that Richelle Mead created is good as it is and I'm okay with it being the end. All I can do now is maybe re-read the books and fall in love with these characters all over.<br><br><br><a href="http://s1175.photobucket.com/user/bookwormstephanie/media/GIFS/tumblr_mtq0w0aRtB1rmkupgo1_500_zpsquehhac8.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428254817ra/14395889.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mtq0w0aRtB1rmkupgo1_500_zpsquehhac8.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1185653713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3916436687020811609">This review was also posted <a href='http://herbookthoughts.reads-it.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE.</a><br/><br/>
  <strong>OH MY GOD. I can't believe it's over.</strong>
<br/><br/><em>It's hard, really. It's difficult to say goodbye to the characters I've grown to love. </em>I love how thoroughly invested I was with these books. It was just too easy for me to care for them because they were really flawed and they make mistakes and stupid decisions every darn time yet still, they are all wonderful.<br/><br/>Richelle Mead wrapped up this series nicely, I supposed, though I feel that this was really short. I would've wan</span>
  <span id="freeText3916436687020811609" style="display:none">This review was also posted <a href="http://herbookthoughts.reads-it.com" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE.</a><br><br>
  <strong>OH MY GOD. I can't believe it's over.</strong>
<br><br><em>It's hard, really. It's difficult to say goodbye to the characters I've grown to love. </em>I love how thoroughly invested I was with these books. It was just too easy for me to care for them because they were really flawed and they make mistakes and stupid decisions every darn time yet still, they are all wonderful.<br><br>Richelle Mead wrapped up this series nicely, I supposed, though I feel that this was really short. I would've wanted to see more Dimitri and Rose. (I love them okay? They're like one of my many OTPs) I need freaking short stories. Or novellas. I might even read some fan fictions because I was left wanting for more even though I was wholly satisfied with almost everything.<br><br>At the last pages I was like...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423433584ra/13624685.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't bring myself to read the end but alas! I reached the last page and the feeling was so bittersweet. I have so much love for these characters and I'm so happy everything turned out okay but I don't know. Some problems were just too conveniently solved and that stopped me from enjoying this book immensely. But I still liked it so I'll still give it a somehow high rating.<br><br>To all those who haven't journeyed with these characters yet, I really recommend this series! (Including Vampire Academy, of course) But if you feel like you weren't up to commit to a lot of books yet, you can at least try to read the first one. You'll never know, maybe you guys will end up loving it like I did!<br><br><a href="http://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadly Darlings</a> | <a href="http://herbookthoughts.reads-it.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Her Book Thoughts</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/margarawrr" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter </a></span>

<div id="review_497225104" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/497225104" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/497225104?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101608159" href="/book/show/24896826-the-ruby-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer497225104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9051822554545756839">Wow...this is it! I'm shocked that I actually read all the books in this spin off. Don't get me wrong, I really enjoy Adrian and Sydney but the problem was that I <i>forgot</i> that a lot of the time. I'm not sure why because I've definitely come to love them as much as I do Rose and Dimitri. <br/><br/>The story begins with someone missing and of course, Adrian and Sydney want to be right in the middle of the action. And who can blame them? Things have been pretty boring at Court. So with a little help, they are</span>
  <span id="freeText9051822554545756839" style="display:none">Wow...this is it! I'm shocked that I actually read all the books in this spin off. Don't get me wrong, I really enjoy Adrian and Sydney but the problem was that I <i>forgot</i> that a lot of the time. I'm not sure why because I've definitely come to love them as much as I do Rose and Dimitri. <br><br>The story begins with someone missing and of course, Adrian and Sydney want to be right in the middle of the action. And who can blame them? Things have been pretty boring at Court. So with a little help, they are off. Naturally, things can't go as planned. <br><br>I did really love the new twist...especially for all its implications. But that would mean, there would have to be more stories and I'm all for that as long as a certain couple (or two, three or four) is involved! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386043186ra/7279157.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The frustrating parts were the times when Adrian and Sydney were apart because they are just sooo good when they are together. Luckily, we get that for the big drama and having both their POVs kind of helps. I love that Sydney needs him as much as he needs her and I really love that Sydney throws Adrian's sarcastic humor right back at him...in the most loving way of course! <br><br>Oh, and I can't forget to mention the exciting familial news! Who would have thunk? I just wish we could have had more scenes about that! <br><br>The new couple? We <i>definitely</i> saw that coming!<br><br>And the epilogue...how amazing was that? I'm so happy that RM pulled it all together and left us in a happy place!<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386043486i/7279209.png" width="400" height="070" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Favorite quotes:</u>
</b><br><br>♥ “So this is Canada,” I said, looking outside my car door. <br><br>“For the last time, it’s not Canada,” Sydney replied, rolling her eyes. “It’s northern Michigan.”<br><br>♥ “Never, ever think like that. I don’t regret anything we’ve faced. Being with you is the best thing that’s ever happened to me, the one perfect decision I’ve made in a lifetime of fumbling and poor judgment. I’d go through it all again to be by your side. Never doubt that. Never doubt how I feel about you.”<br><br>♥ "My life didn't even begin until I met you."<br><br>♥ “Oh, this I’ve got to see, comrade. Dimitri Belikov, badass god, installing a baby’s car seat.”<br><br>♥ “You make me believe anything is possible,” I whispered. <br><br>“I told you before, we’re the center,” she said. “And the center will hold.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="9051822554545756839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I was pleasantly surprised to see that it was mostly him doing it and not just because Sydney was forcing him to do it.<br><br>There was action, drama and a lot of love, the epilogue was perfection, the sense of happiness and calmness that the characters had was really nice to read after everything they had gone through.<br><br>I don’t want to say anything else because I don’t want to spoil anything for anyone. Excpet maybe one thing; Jill and Eddie!! I needed more! a lot more! Maybe hopefully someday we’ll get a story from them.<br><br><br>Keep Calm and Read On<br><br>Instagram and Twitter <b>@bookquotes221</b></span>

Meanwhile, Adrian becomes enmeshed in a puzzle that could hold the key to a shocking secret about spirit magic, a secret that could shake the entire Moroi world </i><br><br><b> I have a big feeling that the big evil in this book is THE WITCH that Sydney tried to kill in Indigo spell </b> And about Adrain's fate in this plot ? <div id="review_554016501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/554016501" />
    <a title="Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18091208-camila-previously-the-opinionated-catruler"><img alt="Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460588276p2/18091208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/554016501?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)" href="/user/show/18091208-camila-previously-the-opinionated-catruler">Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer554016501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3881842206543264242">2019 review - 3.5 stars<br/><br/>This holds up better on a reread with perspective and lower expectations.<br/><br/>2015 review - 3 stars<br/><br/><b>DISCLAIMER: I'm not sure this review makes sense, but I'm just done and too busy reading about the first time Sascha Hunter eats chocolate (which is precious) to change it.</b><br/><br/><br/>YOU KNOW WHAT MAKES ME UNBELIEVABLY, SICKLY EMOTIONAL ABOUT THIS BOOK? Nothing. And that's the problem. <br/><br/><i>The Ruby Circle</i> is okay for a last book in YA series. I didn't expect heartbreakingly brilliant like <i>HP & T</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3881842206543264242" style="display:none">2019 review - 3.5 stars<br><br>This holds up better on a reread with perspective and lower expectations.<br><br>2015 review - 3 stars<br><br><b>DISCLAIMER: I'm not sure this review makes sense, but I'm just done and too busy reading about the first time Sascha Hunter eats chocolate (which is precious) to change it.</b><br><br><br>YOU KNOW WHAT MAKES ME UNBELIEVABLY, SICKLY EMOTIONAL ABOUT THIS BOOK? Nothing. And that's the problem. <br><br><i>The Ruby Circle</i> is okay for a last book in YA series. I didn't expect heartbreakingly brilliant like <i>HP &amp; The Deathly Hallows</i> or <i>Mockingjay</i>, or angrily bad like <i>Allegiant</i> or <i>The Death Cure</i>. But I also didn't expect it to be, well, <i>Breaking Dawn</i>.<br><br> I mean, of course this is better than <i>Twilight</i>. But in many ways, it was <i>BD</i>. Except that's the best of <i>Twilight</i> IMO, and <i>TRC</i> is obviously the worst of Richelle Mead, that I've read so far.<br><br><b>WAYS IN WHICH BREAKING DAWN AND THE RUBY CIRCLE ARE DISTURBINGLY ALIKE</b><br><br>- The MCs are definitely not who we saw in the first book. (Except in <i>BD</i> it kind of is character development, and in <i>TRC</i> it's more like character homicide.)<br><br>- Everyone is there for the party (and I mean EVERYONE), except the mother of the main female character, who is supposed to have a super close relationship with her. But she's like fuck that.<br><br>- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Special snowflake baby they are probably not ready to have yet. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>- And now a toast for daddy issues.<br><br>- <b>There is so much preparation for the final battle, and it's incredibly underwhelming.</b><br><br>- Shit happens that changes the very foundation of a species, but we never get to see how it turns out.<br><br>- So many awesome secondary characters and couples I actually care about that we don't get read more about.<br><br><br>All that said, my biggest disappointment when it comes to this series is that Adrian and Sydney are not the characters I fell in love with in Bloodlines. You know how difficult it's to find an intellectual, thinks-before-she-acts, loyal, believably looking female MC? And a funny, artistic, metrosexual beta male who is comfortable enough with both his sexuality and non-aggressive personality that he doesn't have to prove himself every two minutes who also happens to respect women? <b>The worst thing about this book is that it feels like Adrian and Sydney lose the core of what makes them these complex, lovable characters.</b><br><br> I can forgive boring plots and short, rushed climaxes. <b>But you can't ask me to just ignore that this series used to address mental illness, the oppressiveness of society when it comes to body image, addictions.</b> You can't ask me to forget that rules-lover Sydney gave up her freedom to Abe, the Lord of All Things Illegal, for him to take an eye out of the man who raped her sister. That is the moment her character development started. And <i>The Fiery Heart</i> is the moment it stopped. I have no idea what happened from there. And let's not even talk about Adrian. I can't even go there.<br><br><br>On a different topic, I've seen several people complain about Sydney constantly asking Adrian to stop using spirit and take the meds. And I have to say, ARE YOU FUCKING SERIOUS? I get that it's hard, that spirit is a part of Adrian. It's his power, his drug. One he unfortunately didn't choose. But it's still a drug that is killing him. She's not asking him to stop smoking or being friends with that one chick he hooked up with once. Spirit makes him moody, bipolar (medically, not in a manner of speech). It makes him hallucinate his dead aunt blasting his worst insecurities. It makes him feel like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423703252ra/13661074.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It makes him go from off the roof happy and excited to this in no time, for no reason:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423704089ra/13661147.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And you can't argue against it, because we have seen it happen from his bloody POV. Do you really not remember <i>The Fiery Heart</i>? And the rest of the books, for that matter. Sonya <i>willingly turned into a Strigoi</i>, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Nina went into a comma. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Sydney is not being selfish, she is fucking <i>concerned</i>. You know why? <b>Because the love of her life is going insane.</b> And you know what else? <b>A blameless teenage girl has to go through everything he does without having any say in the matter.</b><br><br>Bottom-line, if I see one more person calling Sydney a bitch for this, I'll cut them.<br><br><br>So, yeah, it was okay I guess. It was entertaining enough, but it definitely didn't live up to my Richelle Mead standards. I don't know how I feel about the very read possibility of another spin-off. If it's going to be like this, I don't want it. This is enough, leave the world be.<br><br><br><br><b>BEFORE READING</b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>4/9 UPDATE:</b><br><br>Not a fan of the colors in the cover, nor that girl's eyebrow game. Or lack of it.<br><br><b>*************************************</b><br><br>"<i>The last book in the Bloodlines series.</i>"<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384252739ra/6826119.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1020089717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020089717" />
    <a title="Dan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11854170-dan"><img alt="Dan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545911764p2/11854170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1020089717?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan" href="/user/show/11854170-dan">Dan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1020089717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3498765458768636943">Overall a good conclusion to an entertaining series. I still don't think Bloodlines is as good as Vampire Academy, but still really good. I thought this one wrapped the series really good, but there were some loose ends and dry parts in this book. Hopefully it'll not be the last time we see the characters that we've gotten to know and love.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3/sZ/PS983+HRsaX1Kv7OOoJXAiYzmuzVO+Im04DZufl3XAuT+M6FyBtcvYjXvHnPFa7wFZD5dQPkc4qg0CUfQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YLAtty0gwlLsP2Moh3CbgNPNC6iFQA7MWCVNd75Cu8BalkRlln4LOksU10lwhZFfBZLsYEvNgKsDWwvGcwFJWg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11289076175150754748">Scorpio Richelle Mead is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of urban fantasy books for both adults and teens. Originally from Michigan, Richelle now lives in Seattle, Washington where she works on her three series full-time: Georgina Kincaid, Dark Swan, and Vampire Academy.<br/><br/>A life-long reader, Richelle has always loved mythology and folklore. When she can actually tear herself away f</span>
  <span id="freeText11289076175150754748" style="display:none">Scorpio Richelle Mead is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of urban fantasy books for both adults and teens. Originally from Michigan, Richelle now lives in Seattle, Washington where she works on her three series full-time: Georgina Kincaid, Dark Swan, and Vampire Academy.<br /><br />A life-long reader, Richelle has always loved mythology and folklore. When she can actually tear herself away from books (either reading or writing them), she enjoys bad reality TV, traveling, trying interesting cocktails, and shopping for dresses. She's a self-professed coffee addict and has a passion for all things wacky and humorous.<br /></span>
